O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, most dear sons, I have completed this book for you which is the last of medical science together with its fulfillment, and I have made an end by its explanations and through its elucidations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is alien to all, so its knowledge has been lost and diminished, and nothing remains of it but small descriptions in books from ancient times that have been passed down by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	From this has come error and vanity, and intentions have become closed off, and knowledge is far away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I must revive it along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition, explanation and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And we will come together with the forms of the instruments for cauterization and other tools required for the work, along with their appropriate arrangement, explanation, and preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of surgery is found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, arms, and their number, and movement, along with moving and resting veins, and where they emerge.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And thus Hippocrates says that the name with its meaning is very important, but it is through action that one achieves little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned earlier should beware lest they make mistakes and harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus, I have often seen many who interfere with this science and so abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut into an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck, and he cut her carotid artery.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	which caused so much blood to flow out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who treated the bladder stone of an elderly man, and the stone was large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he removed with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another surgeon who treated a duke from our land, who had a broken leg with an open wound.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	And the ignorant doctor holds the fracture in place on the wound with strong bandages, leaving no room for drainage, and leaves it like that until healing.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he orders him not to release it.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus, the leg swells entirely, and so does the foot, resulting in its loss.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to go see him, and I hurried to go release his leg.
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I released it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	However, the corruption had already set into the limb, and I could not heal it.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And then I saw another ulcer that burst and then inflamed due to the malignancy of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer, when it is purified of melancholic humour, one should not touch it with an iron tool unless it is in such a place that everything corrupted can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this, dear son, you must know that manual work is divided into two categories:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	That is to say, works where there is danger in many situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I shall demonstrate in each case of this book where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Which is why it is necessary for you to be cautious so that the foolish doctor cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take up your tools wisely, approach your patients gently yet firmly, and employ the best methods so that by God's grace you may bring them to recovery and earn praise.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	Let the dreadful diseases of severe injury pass.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Remove your armor from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may travel from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not treat any illness poorly, or you will be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauterization and other medical treatments for acute illnesses, and the chapters are organized from head to toe.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	And the forms of instruments, and the preparation for cauterization, as well as all that is necessary for the procedure.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping, wounds, arrow extractions, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And this chapter is organized by the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it is organized by the head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Let us recall the work; it is necessary that I speak of the quality of aid and harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and its harm, is a long and subtle art and secret knowledge.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And many wise people have spoken of this and agreed upon it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And their words suffice for me, for I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally all constitutions where there is matter, except for two constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	That is to say, hot constitution without matter, and dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In the combination of hot and dry constitution with matter, some argued and said that cautery is of great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That cautery is not beneficial for illnesses that arise from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And he who says otherwise claims that cauterization provides great relief for hot and dry illnesses arising within the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the constitution of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to these words.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, let not those who have not experienced it intervene, but rather those who understand through long practice the chapter of cauterization, the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, as well as the occurrences and time intervals.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other constitutions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the surgeons assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that fire cauterization is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not burn beyond the member which it heats, and harms no other part if properly used.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medications pass from one member to another, leading to ailments that require swift treatment.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And on occasion, the patient may even die.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fires for their height and because of the goodness of their substance do not burn, if there is no excess to them.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, and it is based on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself for the length of my words, because it does not please me that I take away from you the secret which is contained in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures illnesses of the body, as the philosopher says when demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	take it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, they agreed on when the cauterizations should be performed and chose careful timing.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harmful things coming from below are driven away by cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And especially if the cauterization is necessary for severe pain, acting quickly to prevent a greater evil from befalling the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think of it, dear son, as some foolish physicians do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	For the illness that is healed by cauterization has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	And they say thus:
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	But it is not as they believe, because cauterization is only a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries out the humors causing pain; its value lies in the speed of its action, and the virtue of its work and command.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the illness comes sometimes according to the patient's complexion, and the location of the illness and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and in him are gathered the excesses through eating flesh and similar things unless cauterization is administered where there is little excess and moisture as with tooth extractions for pain and other such things which do not cause a recurrence of the pain.
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and it is indeed so;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is more effective than medicine, but their understanding is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer various treatments for a disease and they are ineffective, then we apply cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauterizations with golden instruments are more beneficial than those of iron, and this was not due to the quality of gold but rather because of its high value.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the skin of the cauterized area does not become discoloured, but this is not true because I have tested it and found that it does happen in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And gold cauterizations are better than those of iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	However, when you heat a golden instrument, you do not know when it is hot by its colour and it quickly cools down.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	They are burned by fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we employ fire cauterization which we have adapted to our practice.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here we have ordered this chapter from head to toe so that the information is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cauterization.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauterizations are beneficial for moisture and cold affecting the brain, and there are two types done due to a disease called "soda", and because of excess humors descending from the head to the eyes, ears, causing numerous dreams, toothaches, sore throats, and especially all diseases arising from cold such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine three or four nights, according to what their condition, moisture and habit can bear.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	And then read again the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on top of yours.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	After that, place the root of your palm onto the root of his nose between his two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And where your two thumbs meet, make an incision; then heat the cautery called 'olivare', of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the marked spot with ink, then move your hand up and down and squeeze firmly while rotating.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift your hand slightly, and feel the place again to see if you can detect the bone underneath even a little bit;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you cannot see it, start the cauterization again until you can see the bone as I instructed;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Afterward take a piece of soft cloth, put some softened cotton inside it, place this on the spot and leave it there for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Then put moist cotton mixed with butter on top of it;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Leave this in place until the inflammation has subsided;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the wound with a preparation called 'Tetrafarmacón', until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients say that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges itself.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, aid is provided.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said one must leave the cautery in place until a part of the bone is burnt, and then remove that which has been burnt from the bone, and it shall be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that the cauterisation should be left on top, and pressed so hard that it penetrates to the bone, just like the 'vertoil' women put in their hair, for this helps the humours to flow out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards, it must be cleaned and sealed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two types of cauterization do not seem to me to be good at all in every way, except for some people who have a sense of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the head [of the shoulder] is weakened by continued natural movements, as we witness in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and likewise when the head [of the shoulder] of the patient is weak by nature, and the first type of cauterization seems more beneficial and effective to me, that is what I use in my work for their well-being.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When any head [pain] becomes chronic and lasts a long time, the patient must use herbs and pills called "cochies," as well as purgatives for the head, eye remedies, and poultices;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if you perform the cauterization as we have previously mentioned, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take heed if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution, and that it is not too cold.
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then cauterize beneath the aforementioned cautery point slightly.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards, cauterize each corner of the head up to the bone, as we have previously stated, and cauterize where it is called "temples".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	And it is there that one places cupping glasses.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	Adjust your hand so you do not see down to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The sick person feels much greater pain in this cauterization than with others, and I will speak of it later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cauterizations of the horns should be more subtle than those for the middle part of the head, and this is the method:
dou cautere dou chief	For cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain occurs in one part of the head and the illness spreads up to the eye, and the skull has been cleaned by purifying medicines, and other treatments that I mentioned earlier for this condition have been done, but with no improvement:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then treat it with two types of cauterization, namely the medical method and that using fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	Medical cauterization is when you take a piece of elm wood, remove the bark and cut it into two pieces that fit together at the skull joints, then split open the temple where the pain occurs in such a way as to be able to place the elm beneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is answered, bind it well and hold it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then undo the binding and treat it with fresh garlic juice, leaving the wound like this for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then apply a cotton cloth soaked in butter as often as necessary.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment, heal it until it is fully cured;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see fit, apply some of the caustic medicines I have written about in the twelfth chapter on caustic medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is performed according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has this shape.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	It is called "close" for the reason that its head is shaped like a bell with one curve and has an appearance in the middle.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, hold your hand and slightly twist it, so that half of the tip of the needle is burnt;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and an abundance of blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterward, place cotton on a piece of cloth, and leave it on the spot for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put moist cotton in butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", use its entire tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this old migraine.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously mentioned in the classification of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the aforementioned cauterizations with fire or iron are not sufficient for him, then you must heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	make a small cut with the knife over that place, making a line half an inch long, and remove your hand once, and press the knife so you do not sever an artery nor reach as far as the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and be careful not to hit the jaw bone when you press it down, and let no air enter that would make him choke or bring spasms upon the patient, and protect against the dangerous evacuation of blood from an artery once severed, a cut which is feared especially by those unstudied and inexperienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	And leave the work halfway through.
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	But I will tell you how to staunch blood when the artery is severed, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the illness and the patient is still suffering, cauterize it again in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you observe this, apply the cauterization we mentioned in the chapter on arterial extraction, using the double-bladed cautery tool.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And these cauterizations are better and more helpful than those.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain in the ears due to cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and one has applied solvent medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned before, but the pain persists, then heat this cauterization point called "poin", which takes the following form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Point around the entire diseased ear, or around both ears if the pain is in both, and move slightly above the root of the ear once you have marked the place of incision.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And make X points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	For the torture of the mouth...
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	A wound that must be treated with cauterization is none other than those caused by flux, as we have said in the classification of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And do not apply cauterization to similar wounds that result from dryness and damage to nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of wound that results from flux of pus and purging of the head and gargles, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	One is at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	Place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and apply it above the ear's head slightly below the skull's horn, and another one on the temple as long as a thumb.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	Leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burnt.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	It has the same shape as the tool we described before, but it is slightly finer and the knife should be a little thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, leave the wound as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but there is no improvement, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two above the two corners of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one at the location called "vessel," as we said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And it is treated as we said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills that cool the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After treating all other parts of the patient's head, apply the mustard poultice to their occipital bone as described in the chapter on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is the manner of cauterization:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	If you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If the wound is treated thus, it is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if it is not, perform three cauterizations within the head, descending to the neck, with a span between each cautery.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	Treat it as the others, but if you see a need for adjustment, and the patient is suffering, perform one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if necessary, place two others on the two horns [of the cautery instrument], and treat until it is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterization be that which is called 'olivare', as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head must be cleansed of hair and according to what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After cleaning the head of the patient, then cauterize on the head and each horn [of the skull], and behind it, three times along the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly from a severe disease, then treat with four cauterizations along the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let it remain until the deepest part of the heart is burnt, and lift your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment is completed, make sure it has healed, and use the cautery method called 'olive oil', which we previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first modify the brain with herbs and other treatments as we have mentioned in the section on treating severe patients who cannot tolerate medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot endure this, have them gargle and chew often with nourishing meats to soothe the brain.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After that, place the ruler on the middle of the head, and perform the cautery as we have mentioned before, applying it to the vessel and each corner.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and suffering, perform cautery as I have described for those with paralysis and bodily weakness, on the spine of the back and neck, using olive oil in the manner mentioned earlier.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply the subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause is due to melancholy, stemming from excess or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then apply cautery with thin irons as we have mentioned for those suffering paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause is melancholy arising from excess descending into it, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink so that their brain is cleansed, according to what was mentioned earlier in the classification.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After rising, lift up the patient's head;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After making a well-made flaxen pad, shaped like a circle, place it in the middle of their head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And have the patient lie down with crossed legs, ensuring they are well-supported from all sides.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After presenting the flaxen pad, apply some old goat butter.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	Heat it with moderate fire so that the skin can bear its application.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	Remove the circle from inside their head, allowing it to cool down.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for the patient once every week, along with other good treatments, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if you wish to cauterize with points, make many points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then apply moist cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' awe
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe first comes to the eyes through the signs I have mentioned in the section above, then begin and give the patient something cleansing for the head, protect it from all moisture, and make them sweat in a bath many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After this, instruct him to lift his head and cauterize in the middle of the scalp, performing two cauteries on the two temples if both eyes descend together, or one cautery if it descends individually.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	Cover all the veins and arteries below the heart during the entire cautery process, ensuring that the cauteries are long, extending across the width of the temples.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Beware of excessive bleeding, and if you observe too much blood loss, stop the bleeding with as much force as required but no more.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you, concerning the extraction of arteries and incision, the caution with which you must stop the bleeding.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes one performs cauterisation at the space between the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	The body of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the veins of the eyes are old and accustomed, and they lie above the paths, or next to the arteries that appear outside the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that these are cold phlegmatic excesses, then apply the cautery which I mentioned at the beginning, to the eyes from below.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	Perform the cautery in between the head, two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries at the space between the two rear bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	et if there is more need, carefully cauterize it above the eyebrows with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From the body of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the classification, and he does not benefit from it, then give the patient to drink three nights' worth of cock's urine.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king, cauterize his head in the middle of the olive-shaped mark;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two 'clavilis' cauteries on the two temples, a little below the hairline.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the 'clavilis' cautery:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the pupil of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called 'olivare'.
de coi ci est li forme:	from which this takes shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two temples as long as the eyebrows are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not leave your hand there unless until a third of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inwards, prick the eye, and a cauterization is performed according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	That is to say, with fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow back evenly, then place the patient in your care;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After, sir, on paper above the eyes make a drawing that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let it be the beginning of the sign from among the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then put moist cotton in egg white and parsley mush on the eye, then heat the cautery with what is here its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterize on the drawn image that you have signed, dot by dot many times until the heart is burnt at the spot.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the sign of success in this work is that you see the paper curling back and the hairs rising to the height of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moist cotton in butter until the scalding is removed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of healing until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this, the hair grows back, and the skin is softened again, then repeat the cauterization on the same spot as before, just as you did initially;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	If the hair falls out, cauterize it until the skin rises to its natural position, and is even, without irritating or pricking the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning medical cauterization is when you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and evenly, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and quicklime, one third of each, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and let it harden so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the mold you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place some from the eyes on paper.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease is only in one eye, you should operate on that one, and if it's also in both eyes as well;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place underneath the eye cotton moistened with egg white.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the patient's head be in your lap and put your index finger on the medicine, and press it once and move it around every time the patient feels a tingling sensation from the medicine, for they will feel a burning sensation as well.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the tingling has passed, remove your finger from the water and check if it has risen, and look to see if the paper has also lifted as though raised by fire or incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, apply more medicine to the place where it was opened for treatment, until your work is even and your eyes are precise.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place moist cotton soaked in butter until the burned heart is covered, afterward treat the area with an ointment called 'diaphenes' and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to, be careful in your work with great vigilance so that the medicine does not touch the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterward and hairs grow in the eye, repeat the treatment on that spot where it has softened due to the paper, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Afterward treat it until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And you should know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness, and according to this, be your restraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and may the correct path never be denied to one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit it, then you must perform cauterization in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place their head on a healthy shoulder;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	Hold the minister's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or twist his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	Afterwards, apply moist cotton dipped in egg white or parsley juice onto the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After that, heat the cautery iron which is such:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaved at the head like the shape of a vaulted arch, together with which the cauterization should be performed;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one side of the head to the other, and if you notice, it should also look like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nevertheless, this one who is shaved is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Afterwards, press the fistula if it is open, and drain out the pus, then dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, operate on it, and draw out the pus forcefully.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Afterwards, apply the hot cauterizing iron above it, and hold your hand over the cautery with your thumb on top of the eye, so that your hand does not slip.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the grease of the eye, and it corrupts.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone with the cautery at the beginning, it would be beneficial.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, restart the cautery again once more, and another if you need it, then leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after, place cotton soaked in butter on it, and treat the affected area with drying ointment until it is healed, but if forty days pass without healing, apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and treat it according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method of cauterizing a fistula, which none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Examine the fistula, and split the site open.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after place in the fissure one subtle probe of which this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	Et they make it to the quantity of one third of a pound;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	Et hold your hand or paw firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run into their eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And it is necessary to put on the patient's eye moist cotton with egg white or butter;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The lead enters the place of the fistula, and it heals with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, you must administer the perforation to the nail, and restore the fistula to the body of the nail according to what is necessary in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	Cracks in lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often occur cracks in lips called "hairs," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as described in the previous sections, and the treatment is ineffective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place cauterization in those crevices until it reaches the bottom.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat the area of the cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	on abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the uvula, on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes decay and swelling, becomes inflamed, and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in previous sections, but it does not heal:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must apply cauterization according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the botch or hole of the fistula, hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom and behind it;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, after treating it as we have said in previous treatments, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	And if he is cured thus, it is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	And if not, you must uncover the site and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in this chapter.
dou movement des dens	Through the movement of teeth.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it is not effective, then place the patient's head on your lap.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	Afterward, heat the cautery, which will be formed as follows: place a cane over the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	And put the hot cautery inside, holding it there until the patient feels the heat reach the tooth's root.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	Afterwards, lift your hand and resume the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	Afterwards, fill the patient's mouth with salty water, hold it there for an hour, and rinse vigorously.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth becomes confirmed in its place, and the softened gum is restrained, while any corrupt moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	From toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain arises due to coldness, whether from cold air or water, and medicinal treatments are ineffective, then cauterization is necessary according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	One method involves butter cautery, the other fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery is performed thus: take butter from a cow, and heat the end of it with an iron or brass spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Afterwards, take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a pen, soak it in melted butter, and place it on the aching tooth until it cools down.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and so it often happens that its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and apply a hot iron until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauteries with fire are such that you take a rod of iron or copper, and it should be thick enough so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	after heating the cautery, from which its shape will come afterward, place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery has cooled down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be relieved on that same day or the next morning.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter during the preparation of this cautery, and then let the cold go afterward.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make the cautery for whatever jaw you want, and according to your ability;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the shape of the chain:
des scrophules	scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is of cold moisture and phlegm, and it does not respond to digestive medicines, then heat the red-hot cautery which follows after in this shape, and make two openings for the smoke to exit on the other side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and apply the hot cautery to the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the base of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its size, leaving it in place for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put moist cotton smeared with butter on top to remove the burn.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the wound with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails over the channels of the body, especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then the patient must first be evacuated through dissolvant medications.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	Afterwards, apply cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go beyond that point or burn any part of the heart except a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After treating it with fire cautery, perform another cauterization at the neck's junction with the spine, and use the clavicle-shaped cauterizer as described previously.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the site just like we mentioned before until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	Whenever all lung diseases are caused by cold dampness and the patient has no fever or dry cough, and it is a chronic condition, apply two cauterizations on the arm above their armpit.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And another one in the middle of the chest between two nipples.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	Let it be that the cauterization is done with what we call a "clavicle", according to the shape described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see fit, perform cauterization by pricking with the point, as was described before in the treatment of ear disease;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be up to XXX or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the site as previously stated, apply three-row cauteries in this manner:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for these cauteries to be lighter, do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation:
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, remind the patient of their illness on their back and side.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift up the heart, which is inside the thorax, with two fingers of your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cauterization iron which has two handles; this is its form.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	cauterize the heart until it is pierced to the side, and the form of the cautery will consist of four pieces.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason cautery is performed with the three-pointed cauterizer, which creates six shapes of cauterization.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves, according to their subtle nature, require the form of the three-pointed cauterizer:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and at times it is adjusted on this one nerve so there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Then place the cautery tool and grind it with charcoal;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	afterwards let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is properly healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again soon after, then immediately perform a cauterization on the thick part of the collarbone, or many cauterizations at once with intensity.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and excessive moisture arise in the stomach to such an extent that they remove it from its normal state, and catarrh is multiplied within him, and with usual treatments he does not improve, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on their back, and extend their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	make three cauterizations afterwards: one below the heel with an area equal to that of a thumb, at each corner of the square (the four corners are the locations for the first cautery), and two cauteries outside these two sides so that the shapes of the cauterization form triangles, and there is enough space between them such that they do not touch when they cause suppuration;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the cauterization be so thorough that it reddens the two sides of the heart, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without any adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cauterization on the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	And for those who fear this type of cauterization, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach in that place. Prick according to the quantity you wish to introduce;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then cauterize with a total of six "pricks".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the previous condition, once it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver experiences pain from cold and moisture and excessive windiness, to the point that it is removed from its natural state due to excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	The sick are cured of what we have said in division, and it does not benefit them, so the patient must be reminded of their ailment.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	And for the third sign, apply cauterization in this manner and with this design, and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondrium, where the man's ribs come together.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	Allow space between each cauterization equal to the width of a finger.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	Let the length of each cautery be that of your body, but do not press too hard with your hand throughout the entire process.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	Only burn halfway through the heart, and let the patient stand upright on their feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him lie down, and stretch his legs, and lift his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your intention is, then cauterize these cauterizations with the knife, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn through the entire heart, as it would cause drying of the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and do not let it reach the mouth, as the heart is very delicate in that area, and you would cause drying for no reason.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is within the flesh of the liver or the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the membrane, they feel excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And so when this treatment is needed, the patient must be reminded of it on their head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	Then lance the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a rod, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	Cauterize the wound with the hot iron until the core is burned, and go up to the surface, so that the pores are all closed.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment, treat it according to the treatment of linen cloth until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And it is not suitable for anyone other than those who have studied extensively in the art of medicine and whose hands these illnesses have been cured before.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then one may operate boldly, yet it seems to me that leaving [the wound] be is better.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of soft wax
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make several cauterizations with the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take one long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and also as thick and as long as your two fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	Oil the root and place it over fire. Cauterize with one large cauterization between the forearm and neck, and two smaller ones just below in the area under the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	Two more cauterizations between the fifth rib and sixth rib, sloping slightly backward;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery between the breasts, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on either side of the breast outside the cautery that is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not squeeze hard with your hand, but apply pressure gently, as if perfuming.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancients said that no man should use a fire cautery like the barber's, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches this abscess;
