car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut into its root, it will retract back into the flesh, causing abscesses to form as well as decay at that place and a painful illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary that it should be treated little by little until reaching the head, and that nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein, when it is treated and reaches five palms in length or more, a man came to me whose vein extended for ten palms long, and when you cut it, it exudes one stream of pus through an opening, and perforates all the way through so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	The matter inside is evacuated, and medicine is applied to the area for some time to prevent putrefaction, then it should be treated like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein is very delicate, especially when it appears in the ankle joint or foot, where many openings form and it must be carefully treated.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure it, therefore, as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called 'ox disease' in our land because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body up and down, and one feels it move from limb to limb until it tears the skin where it was, and escapes;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is born of the putrefaction of certain humours, just as worms, serpents, and larvae are born in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And one doubts its evil nature, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head, and goes into the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drawn out, one cannot resist but when it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	one must therefore bind the place above and below with a strong tight bond, then press upon it and draw it out, and if the poison is perfect in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is to run into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming towards the eye or near it, firmly pinch below it with the eyebrow, then press upon it and draw it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is necessary to use purgatives on the patient, cleansing the body with soluble medications for harmful humours and avoiding putrefying foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that arises in certain limbs, able to move from limb to limb.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see an ailing woman, who uncovered her arm, revealing a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And after that, I saw it rise up towards the shoulder like a worm, more than anything else, just like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from its place, lodges in the shoulder, then spreads throughout the body, eventually reaching the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then it returned around the body again, as I witnessed.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from limb to limb, because I had never before seen this illness behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had heard that pain could often move from one place to another, but I had not experienced it myself until I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a slender body and her veins were exposed, which made the wind's effects more noticeable.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	It does not appear according to this reasoning for those who are delicate and have moist bodies with covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then bind it above and below tightly, and cut above so that the windiness is forced back into place;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the area.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it as if raising the wind, with foul-smelling pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variations of it are such that some have large spikes, others small ones, while yet others are furry or smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And there are those with two horns, others with tongues, and yet more with parts.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and this one which falls on any limb, it happens in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member of the body it occurs, such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it happens therefore in any part of these organs, and the sign of death which I will tell you next appears to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must be concerned with the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many situations afterwards;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not stuck deeply, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and if there is any damage to the substance above the brain, it appears as a black spot in one or both eyes, along with swelling, redness, dizziness, inflammation, reddening of tongue, spasms, loss of consciousness, and vomiting bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps it goes without saying from the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound moisture white like pulsation, and there is also as burned flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, hold on to the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and you also feel as if it were stuck in a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves with the heartbeat, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrowhead that has not pierced the lung is that there is no foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's complexion changes, and they breathe heavily while rejecting cold drinks.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the intestines, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and he suffers great pain and great difficulty breathing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs of his shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead falls into the stomach, sometimes something undigested may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead falls into the belly, and no excrement comes out through the lower intestine, there is no hope for a cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows continuously, and the patient feels severe pain;
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arm and forearm, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, backbone, waist, thigh, legs, and similar parts are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his arm at the base of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I tore it from underneath the fat of the ear, and she was healed without noticeable injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I extracted an arrow that had lodged in the fat of the eye beneath the white part below, and the arrow was bent, and I could only reach its point towards the shaft, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, all iron without barbs;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The eye healed, and no ill consequences befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I extracted an Arabic arrow from the throat of a Christian; this arrow had barbs.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut away the barbs, and manipulated it until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from a man, which was lodged in his abdomen or stomach area, and I thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I incised above the arrow, released it, and pulled it out quickly, and he did not suffer any ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound has healed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and if the arrow remains inside him, and he does not experience any changes in his natural condition or functions, nor finds any harm in his normal activities.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man with an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound has healed over it;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many similar others.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And extract an arrow from the prince's man, which was stuck in his nose and was slightly leaning towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat him after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found that the wound was quite narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tested it with all my skill but did not feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pressure and pain behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was due to the point of the arrow, so I applied an attractive and digestive poultice there, so that his skin would not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the location of the arrowhead appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster immediately, and the wound healed promptly. The patient remained ill for a long time until they felt the arrow one day inside their nose.
et il le me dist.	And he told me (about it).
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound right away until it opened and I tried again, feeling the tip of the arrowhead that was exposed.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I inserted an object into the wound's opening with that corrosive medicine until the arrowhead became visibly exposed.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And it took almost four months to fully penetrate the limits of the wound, and then I widened the wound so that I could insert the tongs, but when I did, (the arrowhead) couldn't come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you may focus your care on what I do not mention, because a book cannot possibly cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But wise masters compare very few great things, and for what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, to deal with the strange occurrences that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not leave the members where they are stuck, but rather according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Wherever by low place where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which shoots forth from where it enters is an arrow embedded in flesh, and sometimes it may be seen now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it cannot be seen, leave it until the flesh around is rotted away, and its exit path has eased.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it so for a few days, moving it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will appear, and if not, pierce around with an awl so that the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, reaching one of the brain's ventricles, and some of the symptoms I mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not draw it out, but leave it until the wound is equalized after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in bone, and does not emerge from the skin, and the patient remains without incident for a few days, prepare to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded such that it cannot be removed, apply cauterization around the wound as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the site until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is buried inside the body where it cannot be seen, search for it everywhere.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, draw it to any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead, and there is no bone or nerve involved, cut it open until the wound is large enough.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	Draw out the arrowhead if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, remove the flesh that is impaled on them from two sides as best you can, then break or bend back the barbs so that you may draw out the arrowhead.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Be careful not to break the arrowhead as you would then have more difficulty drawing it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is rotten; then pull it out, as the extraction would be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the outflow of blood works against you, manage it as we have said regarding treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And beware of incising the nerve and opening a vein, and find a way to extract the arrow without danger, sooner or later, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Place the patient according to their original position when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help there can be; and if you cannot do so, place him as indicated by the signs before you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	If the arrow came from another part of the body or if nothing is apparent to indicate its path, but you see or feel swelling in the skin where it may be;
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut above until forceps can grasp it, then extract the arrow.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone and widens it, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot exit, leave her there again, then repeat the extraction until it is complete.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it was from the arrow that is in there, push the entire shaft out;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it was bone, and you wish to administer a push, provide an instrument with a groove so that the tip of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	then push it through, and if the arrow is grooved, insert the instrument with its point facing inward to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is envenomed, you must cut away all flesh around it, if possible, and then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is in bone or flesh or in the belly or bladder or ribs and it is close to the surface, you can cut above it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And guard yourself from cutting the vein and nerve, then pull it out, and finally sew up the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Let the treatment continue until it is completely healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles the beak of a bird; see below for its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, depending on the amount of arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed end is also like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	The veins from which one recovers are thirty-one, of which sixteen are in the head; namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins located behind the ears, known as "herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And two arteries that are visible in both temples.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	et two veins that are in the two eyelids, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is within the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two glands which are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, which are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which we commonly treat are five in each arm;
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which lies on the left side, and people call it "the vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	The means is called "phlebotomy," composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; laymen call it "vein of the heart.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilic vein is found on the right side and laymen call it "vein of the belly"; it's located above the clavicle and is easily seen as a prominent vessel in the arm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	The cephalic vein is located between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	In the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is located below the curvature of the left calf, while the second is found at the ankle on the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nesse", which is located at the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins underneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins which are behind the ears aids in treating chronic catarrh and headaches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a coarse cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then hold the patient's neck with a cloth, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	place your fingers under your thumb, where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, make an incision there.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and insert it beneath the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein upstream, and cut both the skin and the vein completely through twice, and let blood flow out as much as you wish.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then squeeze it and bind it tight until the vein is clean.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already mentioned the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is useful for ancient headaches, and solid ones, and for chronic eye inflammation, and also for the body to produce tears in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the bleeder is as I say.
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And the patient must strain their neck so that the two veins are clearly visible.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	He will feel pain in the artery below your thumb, and then you must lance it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then raise your heart above the vein near your index finger, push the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, along with its cover, just as you did for the other two veins, and allow the blood to flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And afterwards bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have already spoken of their opening and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is just as valuable as the bleeding from the cerebral vein for ancient illnesses of the face, and also for migraine and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "the digger", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, pressing it with your hand or another object, and let out as much blood as you wish.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein so that it is tight but not too tight, making sure to cover a wide area with your work.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, the blades must not be too sharp.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And if the wound is crooked, because the bone is close by, and sometimes breaks the blade when it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples aids the eyes, and treats inflammation, redness, itching in the eye, and diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting with a cloth, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then you bleed him, and let the bleeding be transverse, a little across the breadth of the blade, and a bit long, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is delicate, perhaps it breaks;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then let the blood flow until you have enough, then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The bleeding of the nose is useful for fever, and acute madness, and illnesses of the head, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is an old ailment;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient tightens their neck, then pulls their nose towards your left hand, and you take the fine long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily there, and now the blood will begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep inside, let the blood flow according to your necessity, then leave it overnight, for it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two jugulars aids in reducing swelling of the neck, and at the beginning of inflammation, and for many illnesses, impetigo, scabies, shingles, and abscesses.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck beneath one or other jugular, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the masters be upon the head of the patient and have the patient sit on a chair. Then bleed at the vein in the neck, slightly wide, then draw blood according to need.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then remake it on the other vein, then untie the knot, and compress both veins moderately, so that the patient does not suffocate.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave it like this until morning, until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The draining of veins from above helps with glue in the mouth, and gum corruption, and lip cracks, and from the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the procedure for healing is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I have explained;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, you will recognize them by their black color, and also by the small dark veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore cauterize both of them, and if you do not recognize them or are unsure, then cauterize the larger one on each side; treat all four veins in this way since it is the same procedure for all.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of veins beneath the tongue aids after the bleeding of the carotid artery, and it is used for narrowing the throat, and diseases of the eye, and ailments of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and they lift their tongue, and look beneath at each side for a black vein;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	bleed one and then the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by piercing with a quick, broad-bladed knife, or a slender olivewood one as sharp as a lancet, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is so widespread as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open up narrow veins that are full of thick blood, and those that contain turbulent blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of an olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	it is more pointed and sharp, and it is used to bleed delicate veins, where there is thin, yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in treating illnesses that affect areas below the throat, and those relating to the neck, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the bleeder must bleed gently, and take care to avoid the artery which lies underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if the artery is severed, and blood flows out uncontrollably, it must be stanched as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And must not be pressed on the flame but cut like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if basilic does not open clearly, you must extract it, and change to another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you desire any vein of it, or you heal in its place the wound between the arm [and another body part]:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cauterize it with the flame of a lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the wound, it is necessary instead that you extend the arm, touching the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the site of incision, then bind the arm, and open the vein with a knife;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and take care not to wound the artery when you see the site swelling, for it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	act quickly then, and apply pressure for some time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if the arm is bound, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient's arm;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it remain still with fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and you faint, and no medic is present, then quickly cut the artery if it is exposed, for this will stem the flow.
et estainche li sans.	Stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of ficus bark, split it, then take one half and bind it on firmly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the bleeding stops, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	But if it doesn't stop, treat as mentioned before with blood-clotting powders.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And cauterization is not always effective in several conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bloodletting of the vein in the middle helps as it releases blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	The person bleeding must take care of the nerve that is below, and if they puncture too deeply, finding the nerve, it may swell and damage, making the procedure difficult or impossible.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	This nerve often appears but sometimes it may be absent in some individuals due to its delicate nature and should therefore be punctured with a fine instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And cut through the nerve with your force.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	Et if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The incision of the cephalic vein is beneficial, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to open a vein by striking at the olive branch or the myrtle branch, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, you must seek the lightest place, and do not press too hard if you miss the first time, and start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, the place may swell in some people when you miss the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your assessment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not intended to cure but rather to maintain health and prevent future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be performed on one of the three veins located on the arm
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, median, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of spring when fasting, and in autumn or winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Bleeding administered for illness has no determined time, but when needed, it should be done at any hour and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	One should not bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman who is pregnant within the first four months and up to seven months of pregnancy.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to bleed the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be done, they must prepare the bowels with a gentle clyster, if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful excess from the intestines which would damage vital organs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One should not be bled if they are overly full of meat or drunk, until the effects wear off, nor those suffering from dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	Nor should one be bled after having suffered a violent bout of diarrhea, or vomiting, or abdominal pain, and multiple episodes of defecation following intercourse with a woman, and from overwork, lack of sleep, and fasting, nor those whose strength is totally depleted by an injury to the arm or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then purify the humours, if the blood is thick, through diet and drinks and with medicine, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to purify the blood and heal the wound around the arm, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself that day against work, pain, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And remain calm and joyful, and let the healer be higher than the patient, and let him rub the arm two or three times, then bind the bandage moderately tight, for if it is too loose or too tight, blood will not flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell up, so that you feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the wound with a drop of old oil, then place your left-hand finger on that area to be incised below where you wish to open the incision, so the vein does not burst and collapse when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like cords when incised, and some are filled with windiness, so that when you apply flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and this is how they are.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if the vein is opened, but the wound is too narrow, thus it is necessary for the incisor to be mindful of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein is opened on the first attempt, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, restart again slightly below this place or above until the levels are even, if they aren't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the levels are swollen, and the patient is frightened, let them rest for one or two days, and do not bind their arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps there will be hot abscesses coming on.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter the bath, then restart the treatment if it pleases them.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the wound is small, or blood trickles out subtly and you doubt it won't be enough to satisfy your need for bloodletting, then draw the flame directly into that same opening.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And do so slightly above this place, rather than below if the levels aren't swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen the wound, and apply a little lard oil, as it lightens the body of blood, and is beneficial for this location where the lard meets the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the lard oil in any wound you treat to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this same property exists in triacle and beef fat when applied to the wound.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	So finely does it separate blood and hinder its flow if too great is the amount.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there is an abscess present of considerable size, which often happens, especially when the wound was not cleaned before but only opened that one time or where the opening of the vein is small, then you must hurry and apply a moist sponge in water and salt slightly warm to the site and bind it tightly for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the release of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days with some blackness or greenness, it will not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, apply something of aloe or myrrh mixed with gallium juice, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there is an abscess and appearance at the incision of the temple:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	remove then that you do not apply anything of what we have said, for perhaps it cuts short of the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but for this wound use a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person's blood according to the quantity of its quality, and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it as thick, leave it until it is refined;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are full and strong, and need bloodletting, make the wound wider, and let the flames be broad;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled often, and it must be done by cutting across, not pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This manner of healing is safe from the loss of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to him whose body requires healing, it is necessary to give moistened bread in pomegranate juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is overheated, then take away blood three or four times; and if he is of a cold constitution, moisten with juice before the healing bread in muscatel syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, nutmeg, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he loses consciousness due to excessive blood loss during the operation, it is necessary for him to drink meat broth and subtle fragrant syrup, and to use other things that we have mentioned in the section on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and perform another operation, it is necessary, when he is weakened by severe bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the amount of strength he has, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding operation, and he has a strong constitution, then he should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to bleed in another part of the body, then he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has much blood within the body which is already overheated, and it brings on fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If a large quantity needs to be extracted, enlarge the opening as much as possible without causing pain.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then you should monitor all the conditions of healing, and keep your hand on their pulse as they heal, ensuring death does not come to them through negligence, which happens many times when healers are careless.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not necessary, when you wish to release the arm and drain blood a second time, with the opening now closed, that you press strongly upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is crooked, do not extend the arm forcefully, as that would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But leave it alone until it heals for a second time.
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Where you point with the tip of the flame until the blood that has frozen in the vein escapes, then apply some wool soaked in warm water, and gently press on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place or in another vein, or even on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is bled instead of the one on the head because it is more accessible.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of cauterization is that the patient must immerse their hand in hot water until the nails turn red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then bind it loosely so that the vein is clearly visible, then cauterize it now across its width rather than its length;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	If the opening is wide and it is cauterized close to the joint of the hand, but blood cannot escape, return the hand to hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not immerse the hand in hot water, as it is done more often in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding from this vein is safer than that of all other veins, as there are neither arteries nor nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding from the vein on the right hand is worth all diseases of the liver, and here is the way to do it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Immerse the hand in hot water until the vein is swollen so that it may be seen;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the bleeding is done in an oblique manner or completely through the vein, it does no harm;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, completely devoid of flesh, and then place the hand in warm water if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is needed, apply oil and linen to the vein to seal the wound, and do likewise for each tube.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the left hand is good for disease of the spleen, and do everything just as I told you about the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases that affect areas below the waist, such as illnesses affecting the uterus, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar ailments in the hips, legs, and lower extremities.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his injury is such that the patient places their foot in warm water and rubs it over the vein until it bursts, and then binds it above the ankle.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and from there it goes up along the leg with many branches;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	treat therefore that larger branch, or at the ankle, as seems best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the leg, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and treat it across as in cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flame cool down.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot exit, place the foot in water, and let it thoroughly drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you fail to cauterize the first time, repeat it a second time slightly above, as the skin is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not be concerned about nerves, as we have said, and treat the other foot similarly in this manner.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is found above the ankle bone, and its opening serves to alleviate hip pain when hot blood is present.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	The quality of the cauterization is such that the patient should immerse in a bath and then tightly wrap above the ankle for four days by twisting it, otherwise, the wound will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it does open, cauterize it in every way possible for you, using various methods of application.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better that you cut it off because the skin is salty, and many people suffer from this condition.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then feel along any line of the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, taking care to avoid the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	Make sure the blood flows freely until you see it coming out, then untie the binding, and place cotton over it while applying pressure.
ele est maintenant sanee.	She is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	cupping incisions
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or brass, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is performed in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by cutting to draw out blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this non-cutting cupping is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Where there's fire all over, or without fire at all;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation which is done by piercing and bloodletting in fourteen places of the body, among which some are entirely on top, like the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and others are in the middle of the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more on either side of the collarbone;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and one below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and two on each shoulder;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and one over the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and two on each arm;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cups of both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cups of both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw out blood, only small veins that are spread across the flesh, and it weakens no one, just as lancing of a vein is done;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither hot nor cold, in any illness caused by overindulgence, until the body is completely emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to the necessity of illness cupping must be done, or as a habit, then administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or towards its end, and throughout any time in between.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to cup, have such heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who find fullness and redness in their faces, and in their heads, and necks, and darkness around the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouths, and have swollen tongues, and spit out blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see during the night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially when it is midway through the month, we instruct them to undergo cupping after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting from the nose helps with headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventousation is in the place of bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is not suitable for those with a cold constitution to use it, or those who have catarrh, because it does great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal often become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little further down due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventousation on the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason, it is beneficial for narrowing of the chest, and for splitting the channel of the lung, and for colds, and for fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be used briefly, for if it holds too firmly, it causes fainting or stomach upset and heartburn.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation at the two collarbones is beneficial for headaches, eye ailments, migraines, strangulation, tooth root pain, and it serves as an alternative to basilication.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you should instruct the patient to extend their arm and place it under pressure so as not to injure the artery and cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation below the chin is beneficial for mouth ailments, gum infections, and similar diseases that occur within the oral cavity.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it serves as an alternative treatment for diseases of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Swelling in the shoulders is indicative of an illness caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventilation of the armpits is just as effective as that of the three veins in the arm, as it draws blood from these major vessels.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the healer not to make it too perfect, for the skin is bare of flesh and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the anus and ailments beneath it, and it should be large and made of copper, which requires proper suction.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and if by chance it was thin, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it creates large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses for the legs heal evidently, as they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the kidneys, spleen, and bladder, and reduce swelling.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are located at the two sophens, and at the two ankles, yet they weaken the body over time, and bring on fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cupping device is such that you place it first on an empty stomach, and suck gently, then put it quickly, and move it evenly, do not stop until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then cauterize, and replace the cupping devices, and take care in considering the constitution of bodies, for there are some with thick flesh, and others with delicate skin.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	You should only cauterize once, and the wounds must be wide, and one deep incision is enough;
et suce legierement.	And suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it should be tapped twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very dense, it should be tapped a third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to draw out thick and viscous blood, we should only tap once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we must often begin again.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, you should tap it thoroughly, and finish when the heart is suddenly pierced, and for those with a thick and hard skull, and narrow arteries, you must grease the cups of the ventouse with an oil that opens and dissolves.
